\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
detail namespace with internal helper functions 

This namespace collects functions that should not be exposed, implementations of some \doxylink{classbasic__json}{basic\+\_\+json} methods, and meta-\/programming helpers.

\begin{DoxySince}{Since}
version 2.\+1.\+0 
\end{DoxySince}

\Hypertarget{namespacedetail_a917c3efabea8a20dc72d9ae2c673d632}\label{namespacedetail_a917c3efabea8a20dc72d9ae2c673d632} 
\index{detail@{detail}!value\_t@{value\_t}}
\index{value\_t@{value\_t}!detail@{detail}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{value\_t}{value\_t}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum class \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacedetail_a917c3efabea8a20dc72d9ae2c673d632}{detail\+::value\+\_\+t}} \+: std\+::uint8\+\_\+t\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [strong]}}



the JSON type enumeration 

This enumeration collects the different JSON types. It is internally used to distinguish the stored values, and the functions \doxylink{classbasic__json_ad8789d0a365d5afaab61e7492908d8b2}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+null()}, \doxylink{classbasic__json_af355a2b131068acf3d623eb6d80a711c}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+object()}, \doxylink{classbasic__json_a184ba4a6b47e6da3703af19349bd776f}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+array()}, \doxylink{classbasic__json_a007ecebde9a7d40714e300ce0ff52908}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+string()}, \doxylink{classbasic__json_acfe2e3c359b545f8edbb72f6bd78718c}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+boolean()}, \doxylink{classbasic__json_aacf244be5088fb183f4ba21a66af9631}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+number()} (with \doxylink{classbasic__json_a2330e35cda16540058fef090abc709bf}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+number\+\_\+integer()}, \doxylink{classbasic__json_a4de72635745144ee519157d23fe7189a}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+number\+\_\+unsigned()}, and \doxylink{classbasic__json_a8d5bb82dfc8cceae1753b52a588eef92}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+number\+\_\+float()}), \doxylink{classbasic__json_a39e4946a414cc978b88939ed1b343d46}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+discarded()}, \doxylink{classbasic__json_ad650dd5a7e019b970abce3d8864b5654}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+primitive()}, and \doxylink{classbasic__json_a2d3a5f8761bc6f163f4119bddaf7b092}{basic\+\_\+json\+::is\+\_\+structured()} rely on it.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
There are three enumeration entries (number\+\_\+integer, number\+\_\+unsigned, and number\+\_\+float), because the library distinguishes these three types for numbers\+: \doxylink{classbasic__json_ae8505b599e706768a1e0bd6718cc7117}{basic\+\_\+json\+::number\+\_\+unsigned\+\_\+t} is used for unsigned integers, \doxylink{classbasic__json_aba48b0bdee31228a4e19b7c040b6d2a5}{basic\+\_\+json\+::number\+\_\+integer\+\_\+t} is used for signed integers, and \doxylink{classbasic__json_a80a229dbc84c1334171ce9c49c873c56}{basic\+\_\+json\+::number\+\_\+float\+\_\+t} is used for floating-\/point numbers or to approximate integers which do not fit in the limits of their respective type.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
see \doxylink{classbasic__json_ae2d5bc42270881ed3e219e8b1456fec5}{basic\+\_\+json\+::basic\+\_\+json(const value\+\_\+t value\+\_\+type)} -- create a JSON \doxylink{namespacedetail_a47b1bb0bbd3596589ed9187059c312efa2063c1608d6e0baf80249c42e2be5804}{value} with the default \doxylink{namespacedetail_a47b1bb0bbd3596589ed9187059c312efa2063c1608d6e0baf80249c42e2be5804}{value} for a given type
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxySince}{Since}
version 1.\+0.\+0 
\end{DoxySince}

\index{detail@{detail}!hash@{hash}}
\index{hash@{hash}!detail@{detail}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{hash()}{hash()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Basic\+Json\+Type $>$ \\
std\+::size\+\_\+t detail\+::hash (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Basic\+Json\+Type \&}]{j }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



hash a JSON value 

The hash function tries to rely on std\+::hash where possible. Furthermore, the type of the JSON value is taken into account to have different hash values for null, 0, 0U, and false, etc.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Basic\+Json\+Type} & \doxylink{classbasic__json}{basic\+\_\+json} specialization \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em j} & JSON value to hash \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
hash value of j 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{detail@{detail}!operator$<$@{operator$<$}}
\index{operator$<$@{operator$<$}!detail@{detail}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator$<$()}{operator<()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily bool detail\+::operator$<$ (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacedetail_a917c3efabea8a20dc72d9ae2c673d632}{value\+\_\+t}}}]{lhs,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacedetail_a917c3efabea8a20dc72d9ae2c673d632}{value\+\_\+t}}}]{rhs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [noexcept]}}



comparison operator for JSON types 

Returns an ordering that is similar to Python\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item order\+: null \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} boolean \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} number \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} object \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} array \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} string \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} binary
\item furthermore, each type is not smaller than itself
\item discarded values are not comparable
\item binary is represented as a b\"{}\"{} string in python and directly comparable to a string; however, making a binary array directly comparable with a string would be surprising behavior in a JSON file.
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxySince}{Since}
version 1.\+0.\+0 
\end{DoxySince}

\Hypertarget{namespacedetail_a3f0588f1a546b169113e6e1e293168f4}\label{namespacedetail_a3f0588f1a546b169113e6e1e293168f4} 
\index{detail@{detail}!to\_chars@{to\_chars}}
\index{to\_chars@{to\_chars}!detail@{detail}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{to\_chars()}{to\_chars()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Float\+Type $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{json_8hpp_a5f2aaec3b681d0a72f7d6e90b70cdcd1}{JSON\+\_\+\+HEDLEY\+\_\+\+RETURNS\+\_\+\+NON\+\_\+\+NULL}} char \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} detail\+::to\+\_\+chars (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{char \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{first,  }\item[{const char \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{last,  }\item[{Float\+Type}]{value }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



generates a decimal representation of the floating-\/point number value in \mbox{[}first, last). 

The format of the resulting decimal representation is similar to printf\textquotesingle{}s g format. Returns an iterator pointing past-\/the-\/end of the decimal representation.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The input number must be finite, i.\+e. NaN\textquotesingle{}s and Inf\textquotesingle{}s are not supported. 

The buffer must be large enough. 

The result is NOT null-\/terminated. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{unescape()}{unescape()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename String\+Type $>$ \\
static void detail\+::unescape (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{String\+Type \&}]{s }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}



string unescaping as described in RFC 6901 (Sect. 4) 


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em s} & string to unescape \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
unescaped string
\end{DoxyReturn}
Note the order of escaping \"{}\texorpdfstring{$\sim$}{\string~}1\"{} to \"{}/\"{} and \"{}\texorpdfstring{$\sim$}{\string~}0\"{} to \"{}\texorpdfstring{$\sim$}{\string~}\"{} is important.
